Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Min' in Talaq Delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of 'min' in tafwid al-talaq and state the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
The partitive 'min' limits delegation; the explanatory 'min' allows full three — a single preposition changes the ruling.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband delegates the power to divorce to his wife, his wording determines her authority. The phrase 'divorce yourself from three' triggers an intra-Hanafi dispute: does 'min' mean she can only take a part, or does it merely explain the maximum? This lesson unpacks the linguistic debate between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and shows how a single preposition determines whether a woman can divorce herself three times or only less.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested element
Locate the precise linguistic point of disagreement in the husband's statement. It revolves around the preposition 'min' (from).
Focus on the grammatical function, not the legal outcome yet.
2
State each imam's position
Abu Hanifa holds that 'min' is partitive (li al-tab'eed), so she can only divorce less than three. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'min' is explanatory (li al-bayan), so she can divorce three.
Note that both positions are from the same school.
3
Examine the linguistic proof
For Abu Hanifa, the primary meaning of 'min' is partitive. For the Sahibayn, 'min' can be explanatory, as in the Quranic verse 'فاجتنبوا الرجس من الأوثان' (avoid the filth of idols) where 'min' explains the filth.
Both interpretations are linguistically valid; no external proof is given.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the wife chooses to pronounce three divorces, under Abu Hanifa only one or two take effect, while under the Sahibayn all three take effect.
This affects whether a triple talaq occurs.
5
Note the secondary dispute on niyya
The passage mentions a related debate: whether the husband's intention (niyya) is required when delegating quantity (qadr) as opposed to quality (kayf). In 'Kashf al-Asrar' intention is required; in 'Fath al-Ghaffar' it is not, because quantity is unambiguous.
This shows how the type of delegation affects other rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي : طلقي نفسك من ثلاث ما شئت، لها أن تطلق ما دونها لا ثلاثاً هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ لأنَّ من للتّبعيض، وعندهما : لها أن تطلق نفسها ثلاثاً، فتكون من للبيان. وهل تشترط في هذا التفويض نيّة الزوج كما في كيف، فذكر في «كشف الأسرار» و «شرح «المنار» لصاحب الدر المختار اشتراطها واستظهر صاحب «البحر» في شرحه للمنار» المسمّى بـ«فتح الغفار» عدمه ؛ لأنّ المفوض إليها القدر فقط ، وله أفراد فلا إبهام، بخلاف كيف.
And in: 'Divorce yourself from three whatever you wish', she may divorce less than three, not three, according to Abu Hanifa because 'min' is for partitive; and according to the two, she may divorce herself three, so 'min' is for explanation. And is the husband's intention required in this delegation as in 'kayf'? It is mentioned in 'Kashf al-Asrar' and 'Sharh al-Manar' by the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar that it is required, and the author of 'al-Bahr' in his commentary on 'al-Manar' called 'Fath al-Ghaffar' preferred its absence because what is delegated is the quantity only, which has individuals, so there is no ambiguity, unlike 'kayf'.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of 'min' in the husband's statement 'Divorce yourself from three whatever you wish.' Abu Hanifa holds that 'min' is partitive (li al-tab'eed), meaning the wife can only divorce a part of three (i.e., one or two), not all three. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'min' is explanatory (li al-bayan), so she can divorce three as well; the number merely specifies the maximum range. The passage then discusses whether the husband's intention (niyya) is required in this delegation when the quantity is specified, drawing a comparison with delegation using 'kayf' (how). In 'Kashf al-Asrar' and 'Sharh al-Manar' it is stated that intention is required, but the author of 'al-Bahr' in 'Fath al-Ghaffar' preferred that it is not required because the quantity delegated here is unambiguous (it has definite individuals: one, two, three), unlike the vague case of 'kayf' which refers to quality.

Key Terms
من للتبعيض (min li al-tab'eed): The partitive 'min' indicating a part of a whole; here it restricts the delegation to a portion of three.
من للبيان (min li al-bayan): Explanatory 'min' clarifying the preceding term; here it indicates that 'three' is the maximum count.
تفويض القدر (tafwid al-qadr): Delegation of the quantity (number) of divorces, as opposed to quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) It depends on her intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi tafwid al-talaq, the interpretation of 'min' determines whether the wife can effect a full triple talaq or only a partial one — a single preposition is decisive.

The Meaning of 'min' in Divorce Delegation: Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'min' in delegation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on the interpretation of 'min' in divorce delegation and apply the principle of taking the certain over the probable to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The particle 'min' is ambiguous between partition and clarification; the certain meaning (partition) is preferred over the probable.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: when a husband says to his wife 'Divorce yourself from three as you wish,' what is the scope of her power? Abu Hanifa limits it to less than three because 'min' means partition; the Sahibayn allow three because 'min' means clarification. The dispute hinges on the linguistic meaning of 'min' and the principle of taking the certain over the probable. We will unpack the arguments and the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the delegation phrase and legal context
The husband says 'tallaqi nafsak min thalath ma shi't'. This is a delegation (tafwid) giving the wife the power to divorce herself. The scope of that power depends on the particle 'min'.
Delegation in Hanafi fiqh is valid and the wife's divorce is effective.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa: 'min' indicates partition (tab'id), so the wife may divorce once or twice, but not three. Sahibayn: 'min' indicates clarification (bayan), so the wife may divorce three times.
Both agree that some divorce occurs by agreement; the disagreement is over maximum number.
3
Analyse the linguistic argument for each
The Quran uses 'min' for both: 'fajtanibu al-rijsa min al-awthan' (clarification) and 'faqrau ma tayassara min al-Quran' (partition). Abu Hanifa argues that partition is the true meaning (haqiqah); Sahibayn argue clarification is also valid and intended here.
The passage notes that 'min' for partition is counted as haqiqah by jurists.
4
Apply the tarjih principle: certain vs probable
The Hanafi response (qulna) argues: if 'min' is for clarification, the wife may divorce three (probable). If for partition, she may divorce less than three (certain). Taking the certain (less than three) is preferred over the probable (three).
This is the core of Abu Hanifa's tarjih: al-akhdhu bil-yaqin awla.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the wife divorces herself three times, under Abu Hanifa it is invalid and only one or two divorces count (depending on her actual intention). Under Sahibayn it is valid as three. Later fatwa often adopts Sahibayn's view for ease.
The text itself supports Abu Hanifa, but mufta bihi may vary in later practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ردت ارتد . وفي : طلقي نفسك من ثلاث ما شئت، لها أن تطلق ما دونها لا ثلاثاً هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ؛ لأنَّ من للتَّبعيض، وعندهما : لها أن تطلق نفسها ثلاثاً، فتكون من للبيان. يقع شيء بالاتفاق، بخلاف كيف شئت ؟ فإنّه إن لم تشأ شيئاً يقعُ واحد رجعي عنده ، ووجه الفرق : أنّ كم اسم للعدد المبهم، وما شئت أيضاً تعميم للعدد ، فالمعنى: أي عدد شئت، والواحد أيضاً عدد في اصطلاح الفقهاء، فكان التفويض في نفس العدد، والواقع ليس إلا العدد، فلا يمكن وقوع واحد أيضاً بدون مشيئتها ، بخلاف كيف، فإنّ المفوّض هناك الحال لا العدد، كذا في العدد.
وهل تشترط في هذا التفويض نيّة الزوج كما في كيف، فذكر في «كشف الأسرار» (۱) و «شرح «المنار» لصاحب الدر المختار اشتراطها واستظهر صاحب «البحر» في شرحه للمنار» المسمّى بـ«فتح الغفار» عدمه ؛ لأنّ المفوض إليها القدر فقط ، وله أفراد فلا إبهام، بخلاف كيف.
[1] قوله : وإن ردّت ؛ أي صراحة بأن قالت لا أطلق ، أو دلالة بأن أتت بما يفيد الإعراض كالقيام والنوم.
[٢]قوله : ارتد؛ فيبطل خيارها ، وذلك لأنه تمليك حالي لا يبقى بعدما ردّ أمره بخلاف التفويض بإذا ومتى على ما مرّ.
[٣] قوله : لأن من ... الخ ؛ لا شبهة في أنّ كلمة «من» الجارة قد تستعمل للبيان، نحو قوله : قوله : فَاجْتَنِبُوا الرِّجْسَ مِنَ الْأَوْثَنِ ) (٢)، وقد تستعمل للتبعيض نحو قوله عال : ﴿ فَأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ) (۳) ، وعدّه الفقهاء من الحقيقة، وجعلوا بواقيها مجازية، وكتب اللغة شاهدة على أنّ حقيقته هو ابتداء الغاية، والبواقي راجعة إليه.
إذا علمت هذا فاعرف أنّ : «من» في قوله: «طلّقي نفسك للبيان، فيكون من ثلاث بياناً مقدما لما شئت، فتملك أن تطلق على نفسها ثلاثاً، وعنده للتبعيض، بناءً على أنه حقيقتها، فلا يعدل عنها إلا عن ضرورة أو بناء على أنه لو كانت للبيان لكفى قوله : طلّقي ما شئت، فلما زاد من ثلاث علم أن المقصود غير ذلك ، فتملك أن تطلق بعض الثلاث لا الثلاث.
[ ١ ] قوله : قلنا ؛ جواب من جانب الإمام، وتقوية لمذهبه، وحاصله : إن «من» إن كانت للبيان تملك الثلاث أيضاً، وإن كانت للتبعيض تملك ما دونه، فوجود الكل محتمل، ووجود ما دونه متيقن ، فالأخذ باليقين، وترك المحتمل أولى.
And if she rejects, she apostasizes. And in [the case]: 'Divorce yourself from three as you wish,' she may divorce less than three, not three. This is according to Abu Hanifa because 'min' is for partition. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), she may divorce herself three times, so 'min' is for clarification. It occurs something by agreement, unlike 'kayfa shi't'? Because if she does not wish anything, one revocable divorce occurs according to him, and the difference is that 'kam' is a noun for unspecified number, and 'ma shi't' also generalizes the number, so the meaning is: whichever number you wish, and one is also a number in the terminology of jurists, so the delegation is in the number itself, and what occurs is nothing but the number, so it is not possible for one to occur without her wish, unlike 'kayfa' because there the delegated matter is the situation, not the number. So in the commentary.
And is the husband's intention required in this delegation as in 'kayfa'? It is mentioned in 'Kashf al-Asrar' and 'Sharh al-Manar' by the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar that it is required, and the author of 'al-Bahr' in his commentary on al-Manar titled 'Fath al-Ghaffar' considered its absence more likely, because only the quantity is delegated to her, and it has individuals, so there is no ambiguity, unlike 'kayfa'.
[1] His statement: 'And if she rejects' – meaning explicitly by saying 'I do not divorce', or implicitly by doing something indicating aversion like standing up or sleeping.
[2] His statement: 'she apostasizes' – so her option is invalidated, because it is a temporary ownership that does not remain after she rejects his command, unlike delegation with 'idha' and 'mata' as previously mentioned.
[3] His statement: 'Because min...' – there is no doubt that the particle 'min' is sometimes used for clarification, like His statement: 'So avoid the abomination of idols', and sometimes used for partition, like His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran', and the jurists consider it as the true meaning, and they consider the rest as metaphorical, and the books of language testify that its true meaning is the beginning of the point, and the rest refer back to it.
If you know this, then know that 'min' in his statement 'Divorce yourself from three' is for clarification, so 'from three' is an advance clarification of 'ma shi't', so she owns divorcing herself three times. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is for partition, based on it being its true meaning, so one does not deviate from it except out of necessity, or based on the idea that if it were for clarification, then his statement 'Divorce what you wish' would suffice, so when he added 'from three', it is known that the intention is other than that, so she owns divorcing some of the three, not the three.
[1] His statement: 'We said' is a response from the Imam, strengthening his madhhab, its summary: If 'min' is for clarification, she owns three also, and if it is for partition, she owns less than it, so existence of the whole is probable, and existence of less than it is certain, so taking the certain and leaving the probable is better.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the delegation phrase 'Divorce yourself from three as you wish'. It opens with a ruling: if the wife rejects the delegation, she becomes an apostate, meaning her option is cancelled because the delegation is a temporary ownership. The main discussion concerns the interpretation of the particle 'min' (from).

According to Abu Hanifa, 'min' here indicates partition (tab'id), so the wife may divorce only less than three times—she can divorce once or twice, but not three. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), 'min' is for clarification (bayan), meaning the phrase clarifies that the number is three, so she may divorce herself three times if she wishes.

The text then contrasts this with 'kayfa shi't' (as you wish), where if the wife does not wish anything, one revocable divorce occurs according to Abu Hanifa. The difference is that 'kam' (an interrogative for number) and 'ma shi't' (whatever you wish) together delegate the number, and since one is a number, a divorce can occur without her explicit wish. In contrast, 'kayfa' delegates the situation, not the number.

A secondary issue is whether the husband's intention is required in this delegation. Some scholars (Kashf al-Asrar, Sharh al-Manar) require it, while the author of al-Bahr (Fath al-Ghaffar) argues it is not required because only the quantity is delegated, which is unambiguous.

The passage provides linguistic evidence: 'min' is used in the Quran both for clarification (e.g., 'avoid the abomination of idols') and for partition (e.g., 'recite what is easy from the Quran'). Abu Hanifa's argument is that partition is the true meaning, so it is preferred unless necessity dictates otherwise. He also argues that if 'min' were for clarification, the phrase 'Divorce what you wish' would suffice; adding 'from three' indicates a partition meaning.

The final response from Abu Hanifa ('We said') is a tarjih: since 'min' could mean either, the certain meaning is that she can divorce less than three (since partition yields a definite number less than three), while the possibility of three is probable. Taking the certain is preferred.

Key Terms
من (min): The particle 'min' used in the delegation phrase; Abu Hanifa interprets it as for partition (tab'id), the Sahibayn as for clarification (bayan).
التفويض (al-tafwid): Delegation of the power to divorce to the wife by the husband's utterance.
ردت (raddat): The wife's rejection of the delegation, explicitly or implicitly (e.g., by standing up or sleeping).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response (qulna) in this passage, why is it better to interpret 'min' as partition rather than clarification?
A) Because partition is the only meaning found in the Quran.
B) Because partition yields a certain number (less than three) while clarification yields a probable number (three), and taking the certain is preferred.
C) Because the Sahibayn's view is weaker in Arabic grammar.
D) Because the husband's intention is always for partition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a delegation phrase uses 'min' ambiguously, the tarjih principle of preferring certainty leads to the interpretation that limits the wife's power to less than the stated number, unless contextual evidence overrides.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Interpreting 'Min' in Delegated Divorce: Partiality or Explanation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'min' in delegated divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the meaning of 'min' in delegated divorce, explain the linguistic reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Core Idea
When 'min' appears in delegated divorce, its default meaning is partiality (tab'īḍ), not explanation (bayān), unless necessity forces otherwise.

In Hanafi divorce law, the formula 'Divorce yourself from three, whatever you wish' raises a crucial linguistic question: does the particle 'min' indicate that the wife can only divorce a part of the three (e.g., one or two), or does it clarify that she can divorce all three? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and shows how the Imam's preference for the literal meaning leads to a ruling that restricts the wife's authority. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze how subtle linguistic nuances can have major practical consequences in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Formula
First, locate the precise phrase the husband uses: 'Divorce yourself from three, whatever you wish' (طلقي نفسك من ثلاث ما شئت). The key is the word 'من' (min).
2
State the Two Positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that 'من' literally means partiality (tab'īḍ), so the wife can only divorce fewer than three. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue it means explanation (bayān), allowing up to three divorces.
3
Analyze the Linguistic Proofs
The Imam's proof: (a) 'من' is intrinsically for tab'īḍ; one should not deviate without necessity. (b) If it were for bayān, the phrase 'من ثلاث' would be redundant since 'طلقي ما شئت' already suffices. The Sahibayn counter: 'من ثلاث' clarifies the unspecified 'ما شئت', so no redundancy.
4
Understand the Hanafi Response (Tarjih)
The text's response ('قلنا') summarizes: the whole (three divorces) is probable—it could be intended or not—while the part (fewer than three) is certain (since the wife must divorce at least one). Acting on the certain and leaving the probable is legally preferable.
5
Apply the Practical Consequence
If the wife actually pronounces three divorces, the Sahibayn consider all three effective, making her irrevocably divorced. The Imam considers only fewer than three (likely one), so revocable divorce remains. The fatwa in this text follows the Imam's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب التفويض والأمر باليد والمشيئة قلنا : الكل محتمل، والبعض متيقن، فيحمل عليه. عندهما «ثلاث ما شئت»، إذا علمت هذا فاعرف أنّ : «من» في قوله: «طلّقي نفسك من ثلاث» للبيان، فيكون من ثلاث بياناً مقدما لما شئت، فتملك أن تطلق على نفسها ثلاثاً، وعنده للتبعيض، بناءً على أنه حقيقتها، فلا يعدل عنها إلا عن ضرورة أو بناء على أنه لو كانت للبيان لكفى قوله : طلّقي ما شئت، فلما زاد من ثلاث علم أن المقصود غير ذلك ، فتملك أن تطلق بعض الثلاث لا الثلاث. [١] قوله : قلنا ؛ جواب من جانب الإمام، وتقوية لمذهبه، وحاصله : إن «من» إن كانت للبيان تملك الثلاث أيضاً، وإن كانت للتبعيض تملك ما دونه، فوجود الكل محتمل، ووجود ما دونه متيقن ، فالأخذ باليقين، وترك المحتمل أولى.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Delegation and Command by Hand and Will. We said: The whole is probable, and the part is certain, so it is carried upon it. According to them (Sahibayn): 'Three, whatever you wish.' When you know this, then know that 'min' in his statement 'Divorce yourself from three' is for explanation (bayan), so 'from three' is an explanation preceding 'whatever you wish', and she owns the ability to divorce herself three times. And according to him (Imam), it is for partiality (tab'id), based on the fact that it is its literal meaning, so one does not deviate from it except due to necessity, or based on the fact that if it were for explanation, his statement 'Divorce yourself whatever you wish' would have sufficed, so when he added 'from three', it is known that the intended meaning is other than that, so she owns the ability to divorce some of the three, not the three. [1] His statement: 'We said' is a response from the side of the Imam, strengthening his school. Its summary: if 'min' is for explanation, she also owns the three; and if it is for partiality, she owns less than it. So the existence of the whole is probable, and the existence of less than it is certain, so taking the certain and leaving the probable is preferable.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the interpretation of the particle 'من' (min) in the delegation formula 'طلقي نفسك من ثلاث ما شئت' (Divorce yourself from three, whatever you wish). The question is whether the wife can issue three divorces or only fewer. According to the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), 'من' here is for explanation (bayān), meaning that the phrase 'من ثلاث' clarifies the preceding 'ما شئت', so she can divorce three times. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'من' is for partiality (tab'īḍ), which is its original meaning, so she can only divorce a part of the three, i.e., less than three. The commentary explains the Imam's reasoning: since 'من' is inherently for tab'īḍ, one should not deviate from it without necessity. Moreover, if it were for bayān, the phrase 'من ثلاث' would be redundant because 'طلقي ما شئت' already conveys the meaning; thus the addition indicates a different intent. The response from the Imam's side is encapsulated in 'قلنا' (We said): the whole (three) is merely probable (muḥtamal), whereas the part (less than three) is certain (mutaʾayyan), so it is preferable (awlā) to act on the certain and leave the probable.

Key Terms
من (min): The particle whose interpretation determines the scope of delegated divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the Hanafi text prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's interpretation that 'من' indicates partiality?
A) The Sahibayn lacked linguistic expertise.
B) The whole (three divorces) is probable, while the part (fewer) is certain, and acting on the certain is preferable.
C) The husband explicitly stated 'from three', which forces partiality.
D) The wife cannot divorce more than once in any case.

Key Takeaway
In delegated divorce, the particle 'min' is interpreted as partiality by Imam Abu Hanifa because the literal meaning is preferred and certainty outweighs probability.
